                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.  With different annealing time, the hollow space and the amt. of Sb inside the tube can be easily tuned by the partial evapn. of Sb.  The as-obtained Sb@C nanotubes exhibit excellent sodium storage properties.  The remarkable electrochem. performance results from the unique coaxial nanoarchitecture.  Specifically, it delivers a high specific capacity of 407 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 240 cycles.  Furthermore, a stable capacity of 240 mAh g-1 can be retained at 1.0 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles.  Most importantly, high capacities of 350 mAh g-1 and 310 mAh g-1 can be achieved at large current densities of 10 and 20 A g-1, resp., which represents the best rate performance among the reported Sb-based anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmon6HTiU9LrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linp1EIhLDH2Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpsVOqsrs%253D&amp;md5=19ea4b459ee66a164418399db8b12d47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201505918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Double-Walled Sb@TiO<sub>2–x</sub> Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                 10.1002/adma.201505918</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D4126-4133%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DN.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BBai%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26title%3DDouble-Walled%2BSb%2540TiO2%25E2%2580%2593x%2BNanotubes%2Bas%2Ba%2BSuperior%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BUltralong-Lifespan%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2Band%2BLi-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201505918&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13193&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201505918&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Double-Walled Sb@TiO2-x Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Bai, Zhongchao; Qian, Yitai; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4126-4133</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, double-walled cryst. Sb@amorphous TiO2-x nanotubes are synthesized by the calcination of Sb2S3@TiO2 nanorods in Ar/H2 produced by the hydrolysis of tetra-Bu titanate (TBOT) on Sb2S3 nanorods.  The formation of the double-walled structures could be assigned to the facile redn. of Sb2S3 and the strong interaction of Sb to TiO2.  Such a structure accommodates the vol. variation upon cycling well, then keeps the structure stable.  Meanwhile, this calcination in Ar/H2 also generates a lot of oxygen vacancies in the shell, supported by Ti3+ species in XPS spectra.  They would enhance the charge-transfer kinetics, particularly at the interface.  Thus, the double-walled nanotubes show excellent electrochem. performance as an anode material in the lithium-ion batteries and in sodium-ion batteries, both of which are on the top of the reported list.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrrdrYefF6qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljM0jGwGZXLEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjtlKms7Y%253D&amp;md5=0bb077f676824aae644f1f5f12368294</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE42944J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pei, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb-C Nanofibers with Long Cycle Life as an Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb-C nanofibers with long cycle life as an anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Lin; Hu, Xiaohong; Qian, Jiangfeng; Pei, Feng; Wu, Fayuan; Mao, Rongjun; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal the uniform nanofiber structure with the Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the carbon nanofibers.  Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).  The superior electrochem. performances of the Sb-C nanofibers are due to the unique nanofiber structure and uniform distribution of Sb nanoparticles in carbon matrix, which provides a conductive and buffering matrix for effective release of mech. stress caused by Na ion insertion/extn. and prevent the aggregation of the Sb nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqODsgQsiGAJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljM0jGwGZXLEA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Sb/Sb2O3 Anode Materials Using a Polypyrrole Nanowire Network for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Do-Hwan; Hong, Kyung-Sik; Lim, Sung-Jin; Kim, Min-Joong; Kwon, Hyuk-Sang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional porous Sb/Sb2O3 anode materials are successfully fabricated using a simple electrodeposition method with a polypyrrole nanowire network.  The Sb/Sb2O3-PPy electrode exhibits excellent cycle performance and outstanding rate capabilities; the charge capacity is sustained at 512.01 mAh g-1 over 100 cycles, and 56.7% of the charge capacity at a c.d. of 66 mA g-1 is retained at 3300 mA g-1.  The improved electrochem. performance of the Sb/Sb2O3-PPy electrode is attributed not only to the use of a highly porous polypyrrole nanowire network as a substrate but also to the buffer effects of the Sb2O3 matrix on the vol. expansion of Sb.  Ex situ SEM observation confirms that the Sb/Sb2O3-PPy electrode sustains a strong bond between the nanodeposits and polypyrrole nanowires even after 100 cycles, which maintains good elec. contact of Sb/Sb2O3 with the current collector without loss of the active materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqftRBwYUjUd7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljM0jGwGZXLEA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three dimensional self-assembly ZnSb nanowire balls with good performance as sodium ions battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liao, S.; Sun, Y.; Wang, Jing; Cui, H.; Wang, Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">211</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11-17</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel 3D ZnSb nanowire balls composed of ultra-thin nanowires were achieved through simple self-assembly method based on typical thermodn. in chem. vapor deposition (CVD) system.  The elliptic cylinder-shaped nanowires with cross-section size of ∼25nm × ∼ 10 nm display impressive performance in sodium-ion battery (SIB) application as anode material.  Comparing to pure Sb, ZnSb is advantageous in resisting huge vol. change and possess enhanced cond., which would do much better to offer a long-time cycling stability and rate performance.  Such a small size of the low dimensional structures can further improve the electron/ion transfer efficiency.  Through systematic measurements, we found that, at 20 mA/g, the capacity remains 377mAh/g after the 100th cycle with the coulombic efficiency at ∼99%.  Even if the c.d. increased to 750 mA/g, the value was still higher than 225mAh/g.  The half-cell device also provides a rapid response and stable output in the rate tests (20-650 mA/g).  The good performance originates from the unique structural configuration, implying the huge potential value of ZnSb in SIB application.  We hope the results also can expand the Sb based anode material family.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQUrzEtgymvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljou6VbY_pXYA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVags7nN&amp;md5=6e34b0d48afed2593cd6f95a6751d7e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.04.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Glucose-Assisted Synthesis of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C Composite as an Electrode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Glucose-assisted synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite as an electrode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Guangqiang; Jiang, Danlu; Wang, Hui; Lan, Xinzheng; Zhong, Honghai; Jiang, Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, Na3V2(PO4)3 with a rhombohedral, Na+ superionic conductor (NASICON)-type structure, was synthesized via a solid-state carbothermal redn. reaction assisted by mechanochem. activation.  Electron microscopy anal. showed that the synthesized Na3V2(PO4)3 particles had an av. size of 300 nm, being coated with a uniform layer of carbon 3 nm in thickness.  As a cathode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 98.17 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 2.5 to 3.8 V.  This was owing to the V3+/V4+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaV2(PO4)3.  The cathode lost 4.92% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  As an anode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 63.2 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 1.0 to 2.5 V.  This was owing to the V2+/V3+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and Na4V2(PO4)3.  The anode lost approx. 5.41% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  The three-dimensional channel structure of NaV2(PO4)3 and the changes induced in its lattice parameters during the charge/discharge processes were simulated on the basis of d. functional theory.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqL5W7t4QuZY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljou6VbY_pXYA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXps12lsbk%253D&amp;md5=59ad73ad234d3ab597038123cdf3347c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcat.2010.02.031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guan, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel Synthetic Approach to Synthesizing Bulk and Supported Metal Phosphides</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper presents a novel synthetic approach to synthesizing metal phosphides.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres for superior sodium-iron sulfide batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Yang, Jianping; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua Kun; Zhang, Wei-xian; Zhao, Dongyuan; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8689</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.  The proven conversion reaction between sodium and iron sulfide results in high capacity but severe vol. changes.  Nanostructural design, including of nanosized iron sulfide yolks (∼170 nm) with porous carbon shells (∼30 nm) and extra void space (∼20 nm) in between, has been used to achieve excellent cycling performance without sacrificing capacity.  This sustainable sodium-iron sulfide battery is a promising candidate for stationary energy storage.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Yolk-Shell Sn@C Eggette-like Nanostructure: Application in Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Site; Wang, Ziming; Liu, Jun; Yang, LinYu; Guo, Yue; Cheng, Lizi; Lei, Ming; Wang, Wenjun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Yolk-shell carbon encapsulated tin (Sn@C) eggette-like compds. (SCE) have been synthesized by a facile method.  The SCE structures consist of tin cores covered by carbon membrane networks with extra voids between the carbon shell and tin cores.  The novel nanoarchitectures exhibit high electrochem. performance in both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  As anodes for LIBs, the SCE electrodes exhibit a specific capacity of ∼850 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C (100 mA g-1) and high rate capability (∼450 mA h g-1 remains) at high current densities up to 5 C (5000 mA g-1).  For SIBs, the SCE electrodes show a specific capacity of ∼400 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C and high rate capacity (∼150 mA h g-1 remains) at high current densities up to 5 C (5000 mA g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqt6bjCi8FKQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljou6VbY_pXYA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFOktb%252FP&amp;md5=5113b024b734696642e36fcd67e43313</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2013.02.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oyler, N.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hydrogenated surface disorder enhances lithium ion battery performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xia, Ting; Zhang, Wei; Li, Wenjing; Oyler, Nathan A.; Liu, Gao; Chen, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2, well known for its photocatalytic properties, has also been studied as a safer anode material for lithium ion batteries compared to graphite.  However, improvements are needed to address the limited lithium ion diffusion within the host and the structural distortion during lithium insertion/extn.  Here, we demonstrate that a thin layer of hydrogenated surface disorder on the cryst. TiO2 electrode induces better electrochem. energy storage performance, better charge/discharge rate performance, larger capacity and longer stability.  The reasons for these improvements are explored in terms of the facilitation of lithium ion transport within the disordered layer and the alleviation of structural distortion during the lithium insertion/extn. process, and the faster ion exchange rates in the hydrogenated disordered layer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6hLKanzqYn7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8ZuEinqde6A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXksFaqtr4%253D&amp;md5=6fa0f5d9491cb642f1786f759e1adf4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b01208"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yue, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hydrogenated TiO<sub>2</sub> Branches Coated Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Nanorods as an Advanced Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hydrogenated TiO2 Branches Coated Mn3O4 Nanorods as an Advanced Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Yue, Jie; Chen, Liang; Qian, Yitai; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rational design and delicate control on the component, structure, and surface of electrodes in lithium-ion batteries are highly important to their performances in practical applications.  Compared with various components and structures for electrodes, the choices for their surface are quite limited.  The most widespread surface for numerous electrodes, a carbon shell, has its own issues, which stimulates the desire to find another alternative surface.  Here, hydrogenated TiO2 is exemplified as an appealing surface for advanced anodes by the growth of ultrathin hydrogenated TiO2 branches on Mn3O4 nanorods.  High theor. capacity of Mn3O4 is well matched with low vol. variation (∼4%), enhanced elec. cond., good cycling stability, and rate capability of hydrogenated TiO2, as demonstrated in their electrochem. performances.  The proof-of-concept reveals the promising potential of hydrogenated TiO2 as a next-generation material for the surface in high-performance hybrid electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3BOey-EK18rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8ZuEinqde6A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsVeisrg%253D&amp;md5=01c070e38fd8959adca17464196b7f11</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1116/1.588184"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuen, W.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and Characterization of Phosphated Mesoporous Titanium Dioxide with High Photocatalytic Activity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Jimmy C.; Zhang, Lizhi; Zheng, Zhi; Zhao, Jincai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2003</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2280-2286</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A surfactant-templated approach was used to synthesize phosphated mesoporous titanium dioxide by incorporating phosphorus from phosphoric acid directly into the framework of TiO2.  The resulting materials were characterized by XRD, nitrogen adsorption, TEM, XPS anal., UV-vis spectroscopy, FT-IR spectroscopy, and isoelec. point measurements.  The surface area of phosphated mesoporous TiO2 exceeded 300 m2/g after calcination at 400 °C.  It was found that the incorporation of phosphorus could stabilize the TiO2 framework and increase the surface area significantly.  This stabilization is attributed to two reasons: the more complete condensation of surface Ti-OH in the as-prepd. sample and the inhibition of grain growth of the embedded anatase TiO2 by the interspersed amorphous titanium phosphate matrix during thermal treatment.  Both pure and phosphated mesoporous TiO2 show significant activities on the oxidn. of n-pentane.  The higher photocatalytic activity of phosphated mesoporous TiO2 can be explained by the extended band gap energy, large surface area, and the existence of Ti ions in a tetrahedral coordination.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9syrh4KN_3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8ZuEinqde6A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD3sXjsFakurc%253D&amp;md5=13947f1ff9dd524eef3e603f2d5094bd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1021/cm050646w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Facile Layer-by-Layer Adsorption and Reaction Method to the Preparation of Titanium Phosphate Ultrathin Films</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A layer-by-layer adsorption and reaction method was developed for the prepn. of titanium phosphate ultrathin films.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium poly(acrylate) binder efficiently improves the electrode performance of graphite/silicon composites in TFSA-based pure ionic liq.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase Titania Nanorods as an Intercalation Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Ki-Tae; Ali, Ghulam; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Yoon, Chong Seung; Yashiro, Hitoshi; Sun, Yang-Kook; Lu, Jun; Amine, Khalil; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. activity of anatase TiO2 nanorods in a Na cell.  The anatase TiO2 nanorods were synthesized by a hydrothermal method, and their surfaces were coated by carbon to improve the elec. cond. by carbonization of pitch at 700° for 2 h in Ar flow.  The resulting structure does not change before and after the carbon coating, as confirmed by x-ray diffraction.  Transmission electron microscopy images confirm the presence of a carbon coating on the anatase TiO2 nanorods.  In cell tests, anodes of bare and carbon-coated anatase TiO2 nanorods exhibit stable cycling performance and attain a capacity of about 172 and 193 mA-h/g on the first charge, resp., in the voltage range of 0-3 V.  With the help of the conductive carbon layers, the carbon-coated anatase TiO2 delivers more capacity at high rates, 104 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g), 82 mA-h/g at the 30C rate (10 A/g), and 53 mA-h/g at the 100C rate (33 A g-1).  By contrast, the anode of bare anatase TiO2 nanorods delivers only about 38 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g).  The excellent cyclability and high-rate capability are the result of a Na+ insertion and extn. reaction into the host structure coupled with Ti4+/3+ redox reaction, as shown by x-ray absorption spectroscopy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpadjcIpWM-W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHuWiZ6sffug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXktlGhsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=4bc3a520e6f654a82cbee3b778eef0e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA04995K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Memarzadeh Lotfabad, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kalisvaart, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kohandehghan, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Karpuzov, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Origin of Non-SEI Related Coulombic Efficiency Loss in Carbons Tested Against Na and Li</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">2</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">19685</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">19695</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4TA04995K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D2%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D19685-19695%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DE.%2BMemarzadeh%2BLotfabad%26author%3DP.%2BKalisvaart%26author%3DA.%2BKohandehghan%26author%3DD.%2BKarpuzov%26author%3DD.%2BMitlin%26title%3DOrigin%2Bof%2BNon-SEI%2BRelated%2BCoulombic%2BEfficiency%2BLoss%2Bin%2BCarbons%2BTested%2BAgainst%2BNa%2Band%2BLi%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC4TA04995K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13193&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC4TA04995K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origin of non-SEI related coulombic efficiency loss in carbons tested against Na and Li</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Memarzadeh Lotfabad, Elmira; Kalisvaart, Peter; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Karpuzov, Dimitre; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">19685-19695</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Partially ordered but not graphitized carbons are widely employed for sodium and lithium ion battery (NIB and LIB) anodes, either in their pure form or as a secondary supporting phase for oxides, sulfides and insertion electrodes.  These "pseudographitic" materials ubiquitously display a poor initial coulombic efficiency (CE), which has been historically attributed to solid electrolyte interface (SEI) formation on their large surface areas (up to ∼2500 m2 g-1).  Here we identify the other sources CE loss by examg. a pseudographitic carbon with a state-of-the-art capacity (&gt;350 mA h g-1 for NIB, &gt;800 mA h g-1 for LIB), but with a purposely designed low surface area (14.5 m2 g-1) that disqualifies SEI from having a substantial role.  During the initial several (&lt;5) cycles both Na and Li are irreversibly trapped in the bulk, with the assocd. CE loss occurring at higher desodiation/delithiation voltages.  We measure a progressively increasing graphene interlayer spacing and a progressively increasing Raman G band intensity, indicating that the charge carriers become trapped not only at the graphene defects but also between the graphene planes hence causing them to both dilate and order.  For the case of Li, we also unambiguously detected irreversible metal underpotential deposition ("nanoplating") within the nanopores at roughly below 0.2 V.  It is expected that in conventional high surface area carbons these mechanisms will be a major contributor to CE loss in parallel to classic SEI formation.  Key implications to emerge from these findings are that improvements in early cycling CE may be achieved by synthesizing pseudographitic carbons with lower levels of trapping defects, but that for LIBs the large cycle 1 CE loss may be unavoidable if highly porous structures are utilized.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrS77pE8Yg31rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgHuWiZ6sffug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslGnsrbF&amp;md5=a1179605823e145123e603316b82ac0c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b04225"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hong, K.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nam, D.-H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lim, S.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sohn, D.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The morphology-controlled synthesis of a nanoporous-antimony anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Shuai; Feng, Jinkui; Bian, Xiufang; Liu, Jie; Xu, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have presented a comprehensive study of using chem. dealloying methods to control the morphol. of nanoporous-antimony (NP-Sb) and the size of Sb particles.  For the first time, depending on the regulation of the Al-Sb alloy compn., coral-like NP-Sb (NP-Sb70), honeycomb-like NP-Sb (NP-Sb80) and Sb particles (Sb10, Sb30 and Sb45) with different sizes were prepd. through chem. dealloying of Al30Sb70, Al20Sb80, Al90Sb10, Al70Sb30 and Al55Sb45 (at%) alloy ribbon precursors resp., a top-down process.  The NP-Sb70 delivered a high capacity of 573.8 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at a rate of 100 mA g-1 with good rate capability as anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The excellent electrochem. performance is because of its innovative electrode design, which ensures strong structural integrity, high sodium ion accessibility, and fast electrode transport.  This scalable strategy shall pave the way for the mass prodn. of large-capacity electrodes for SIBs and other energy storage systems, providing new guidelines for the optimization of the synthesis of nanostructures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqGZBR5siNySrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liIL5Xq3WJEnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xjt1ahsrY%253D&amp;md5=afe34d66552e55ad27379ae79c92d3aa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta01324g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nithya, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gopukumar, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">RGO/Nano Sb Composite: A High Performance Anode Material for Na<sup>+</sup> Ion Batteries and Evidence for the Formation of Nanoribbons from the Nano RGO Sheet During Galvanostatic Cycling</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">rGO/nano Sb composite: a high performance anode material for Na+ ion batteries and evidence for the formation of nanoribbons from the nano rGO sheet during galvanostatic cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nithya, C.; Gopukumar, S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10516-10525</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries exhibit high energy and power densities, thereby making them a promising power sources for multifarious applications.  However, the abundance of lithium (Li) is one of the major crit. issues for using Li battery technologies.  Therefore, for large-scale applications a sodium (Na) ion battery is one of the apt alternatives for portable electronics instead of expensive Li ion batteries.  One of the challenging issues in Na+ ion batteries is the difficulty to understand the chem. involved in view of the large size of the Na+ ion as compared to the Li+ ion, which makes the alloying/dealloying difficult during cycling.  Hence, in this present work, we explore an innovative concept of storing Na+ ions in reduced graphene oxide/antimony (Sb) metal composites.  Such a concept of storing Na+ in the rGO/Sb composite is one of the simplest ways to enhance the electrochem. performance of metal-based anodes for sodium ion batteries.  Furthermore, it is seen that the nano rGO sheet transforms to nanoribbons upon galvanostatic cycling, as evidenced by TEM.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGryp-lzHn0P9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liIL5Xq3WJEnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVWrtbbF&amp;md5=0cb4120ef4c51ee603ae519957bf98c0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC05989A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb Nanoparticles Decorated N-Rich Carbon Nanosheets as Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries with Superior Rate Capability and Long Cycling Stability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafast and Highly Reversible Sodium Storage in Zinc-Antimony Intermetallic Nanomaterials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nie, Anmin; Gan, Li-yong; Cheng, Yingchun; Tao, Xinyong; Yuan, Yifei; Sharifi-Asl, Soroosh; He, Kun; Asayesh-Ardakani, Hasti; Vasiraju, Venkata; Lu, Jun; Mashayek, Farzad; Klie, Robert; Vaddiraju, Sreeram; Schwingenschloegl, Udo; Shahbazian-Yassar, Reza</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The progress on sodium-ion battery technol. faces many grand challenges, one of which is the considerably lower rate of sodium insertion/deinsertion in electrode materials due to the larger size of sodium (Na) ions and complicated redox reactions compared to the lithium-ion systems.  Here, it is demonstrated that sodium ions can be reversibly stored in Zn-Sb intermetallic nanowires at speeds that can exceed 295 nm s-1.  Remarkably, these values are one to three orders of magnitude higher than the sodiation rate of other nanowires electrochem. tested with in situ transmission electron micro-scopy.  It is found that the nanowires display about 161% vol. expansion after the first sodiation and then cycle with an 83% reversible vol. expansion.  Despite their massive expansion, the nanowires can be cycled without any cracking or facture during the ultrafast sodiation/desodiation process.  In addn., most of the phases involved in the sodiation/desodiation process possess high elec. cond.  More specifically, the NaZnSb exhibits a layered structure, which provides channels for fast Na+ diffusion.  This observation indicates that Zn-Sb intermetallic nanomaterials offer great promise as high rate and good cycling stability anodic materials for the next generation of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoucDZuJ2iH_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liIL5Xq3WJEnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXitVClt7bK&amp;md5=986c179594055e40130b2c55b59d6936</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC05275G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ko, Y.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cathodic corrosion, a green electrochem. method, has been employed to obtain Sb nanomaterials utilized as anode material for lithium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries.  Interestingly, two different corrosion mechanisms are found, coming from the impact of electrolyte, resulting in the formation of hexagonal and amorphous Sb in aq. and org. soln., resp.  With the help of water-sol. CM-cellulose binder and the electrolyte additive fluoroethylene carbonate, both hexagonal and amorphous Sb electrodes exhibit good cycling stability when utilized as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries.  Addnl., both the hexagonal and amorphous Sb electrodes show very good rate capability in lithium-ion batteries.  Even at high c.d. (2000 mA g-1), the hexagonal and amorphous Sb give reversible capacities of 422 and 379 mA h g-1, resp.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium/Lithium Storage Behavior of Antimony Hollow Nanospheres for Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Hongshuai; Jing, Mingjun; Yang, Yingchang; Zhu, Yirong; Fang, Laibing; Song, Weixin; Pan, Chengchi; Yang, Xuming; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have come up as an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications because of abundant Na storage in the earth crust.  Antimony hollow nanospheres obtained by galvanic replacement were first applied as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries and exhibited superior electrochem. performances with high reversible capacity of 622.2 mA-h/g at a c.d. of 50 mA/g after 50 cycles, close to the theor. capacity (660 mA-h/g); even at high c.d. of 1600 mA/g, the reversible capacities can also reach 315 mA-h/g.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical properties and morphological evolution of pitaya-like Sb@C microspheres as high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Lin; Lu, Haiyan; Xiao, Lifen; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pitaya-like Sb@C microspheres are prepd. successfully by facile aerosol spray drying synthesis.  Structural and morphol. characterizations reveal that the Sb@C microspheres have a uniform pitaya-like structure, with well crystd. Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the C matrix.  The Sb@C microsphere electrodes exhibit high Na storage capacity of 655 mA h g-1 at C/15 with excellent cyclability (93% of capacity retention over 100 cycles), as well as good rate capability.  Also, the morphol. evolution of the Sb@C microspheres is studied to account for its excellent electrochem. performance, caused by maintenance of the pitaya-like configuration during cycling.  This structural stability guarantees tight contact of Sb with C buffer, as well as uniform distribution of Sb to balance the localized mech. stress, ensuring excellent electrochem. performance.  The structural design and synthetic method reported in this work may provide an effective way to stabilize electrochem. performance of Na-storable alloy materials and therefore provide a new prospect for creation of cycle-stable alloy anodes for high capacity Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo57lFV_VztT7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWxXhJBJfYKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1ejtLc%253D&amp;md5=674765846a598100cc65c5cd27bf938d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA04703J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cypress Leaf-like Sb as Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (P) have been considered as one of the most promising anode material for both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (NIBs), because of its high theor. capacity.  However, natural insulating property and the large vol. expansion of red P during cycling lead to poor cyclability and low rate performance, which prevents its practical application.  Here, the lithium storage and sodium storage performance of red P is significantly improved by confining nanosized amorphous red P into the mesoporous carbon matrix (P@CMK-3) using a vaporization-condensation-conversion process.  The P@CMK-3 shows a high reversible specific capacity of ∼2250 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P at 0.25 C (∼971 mA h g-1 based on the composite), excellent rate performance of 1598 and 624 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P at 6.1 and 12 C, resp. (562 and 228 mA h g-1 based on the mass of the composite at 6.1 and 12 C, resp.), and significantly enhanced cycle life of 1150 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P at 5 C (500 mA h g-1 based on the mass of the composite) after 1000 cycles for LIBs.  For Na ions, it also displays a reversible capacity of 1020 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P (370 mA h g-1 based on the mass of the composite) after 210 cycles at 5C.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-performance symmetric sodium-ion batteries using a new, bipolar O3-type material, Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Shaohua; Yu, Haijun; Liu, Pan; Ren, Yang; Zhang, Tao; Chen, Mingwei; Ishida, Masayoshi; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Based on low-cost and rich resources, sodium-ion batteries have been regarded as a promising candidate for next-generation energy storage batteries in the large-scale energy applications of renewable energy and smart grids.  However, there are some crit. drawbacks limiting its application, such as safety and stability problems.  In this work, a stable sym. sodium-ion battery based on the bipolar, active O3-type material, Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2, is developed.  This bipolar material shows a typical O3-type layered structure, contg. two electrochem. active transition metals with redox couples of Ni4+/Ni2+ and Ti4+/Ti3+, resp.  This Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2-based sym. cell exhibits a high av. voltage of 2.8 V, a reversible discharge capacity of 85 mA h g-1, 75% capacity retention after 150 cycles and good rate capability.  This full sym. cell will greatly contribute to the development of room-temp. sodium-ion batteries with a view towards safety, low cost and long life, and it will stimulate further research on sym. cells using the same active materials as both cathode and anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqmF3B7AwSKZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5OTSvtC7sJg"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Beyond Li-ion: electrode materials for sodium- and magnesium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Masse, Robert C.; Uchaker, Evan; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science China Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The need for economical and sustainable energy storage drives battery research today.  While Li-ion batteries are the most mature technol., scalable electrochem. energy storage applications benefit from redns. in cost and improved safety.  Sodium- and magnesium-ion batteries are two technologies that may prove to be viable alternatives.  Both metals are cheaper and more abundant than Li, and have better safety characteristics, while divalent magnesium has the added bonus of passing twice as much charge per atom.  On the other hand, both are still emerging fields of research with challenges to overcome.  For example, electrodes incorporating Na+ are often pulverized under the repeated strain of shuttling the relatively large ion, while insertion and transport of Mg2+ is often kinetically slow, which stems from larger electrostatic forces.  This review provides an overview of cathode and anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, and a comprehensive summary of research on cathodes for magnesium-ion batteries.  In addn., several common exptl. discrepancies in the literature are addressed, noting the addnl. constraints placed on magnesium electrochem.  Lastly, promising strategies for future study are highlighted.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqeu1nepe2jR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgnbeW1nmBD9A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslCqtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=54ef894bc82bd710e90a1c23bb069d40</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1149/1.1379565"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stevens, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been considered as promising alternatives to Li-ion batteries due to the natural abundance of sodium resources.  Searching for high-performance anode materials currently becomes a hot topic and also a great challenge for developing Na-ion batteries.  In this work, a novel hybrid anode is synthesized consisting of ultrafine, few-layered SnS2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile solvothermal route. The hybrid can also sustain a c.d. up to 12.8 A/g (≈28C) where the charge process can be completed in only 1.3 min while still delivering a charge capacity of 337 mA-h/g.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report colloidal synthesis of Sb nanocrystals with mean size tunable in the 10-20 nm range and with narrow size distributions of 7-11%.  In comparison to microcryst. Sb, 10 and 20 nm Sb nanocrystals exhibit enhanced rate capability and higher cycling stability as anode materials in rechargeable Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  All three particle sizes of Sb have high and similar Li-ion and Na-ion charge storage capacities of 580-640 mA-h/g at moderate charging/discharging current densities of 0.5-1C (1C rate is 660 mA/g).                         rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coupling In Situ TEM and Ex Situ Analysis to Understand Heterogeneous Sodiation of Antimony</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhi; Tan, Xuehai; Li, Peng; Kalisvaart, Peter; Janish, Matthew T.; Mook, William M.; Luber, Erik J.; Jungjohann, Katherine L.; Carter, C. Barry; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We employed an in situ electrochem. cell in the transmission electron microscope (TEM) together with ex situ time-of-flight, secondary-ion mass spectrometry (TOF-SIMS) depth profiling, and FIB-helium ion scanning microscope (HIM) imaging to detail the structural and compositional changes assocd. with Na/Na+ charging/discharging of 50 and 100 nm thin films of Sb.  TOF-SIMS on a partially sodiated 100 nm Sb film gives a Na signal that progressively decreases toward the current collector, indicating that sodiation does not proceed uniformly.  This heterogeneity will lead to local volumetric expansion gradients that would in turn serve as a major source of intrinsic stress in the microstructure.  In situ TEM shows time-dependent buckling and localized sepn. of the sodiated films from their TiN-Ge nanowire support, which is a mechanism of stress-relaxation.  Localized horizontal fracture does not occur directly at the interface, but rather at a short distance away within the bulk of the Sb.  HIM images of FIB cross sections taken from sodiated half-cells, elec. disconnected, and aged at room temp., demonstrate nonuniform film swelling and the onset of analogous through-bulk sepn.  TOF-SIMS highlights time-dependent segregation of Na within the structure, both to the film-current collector interface and to the film surface where a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) exists, agreeing with the electrochem. impedance results that show time-dependent increase of the films' charge transfer resistance.  We propose that Na segregation serves as a secondary source of stress relief, which occurs over somewhat longer time scales.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGob2HLjqRKWnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljnnkRN9docAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFagtLvN&amp;md5=6c30a8cf04ee0cc7d664d3209bd6864d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE00878F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Large-scale Highly Ordered Sb Nanorod Arrays Anode with High Capacity and Rate Capability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are a potential substitute to Li-ion batteries for energy storage devices.  However, their poor electrochem. performance, esp. capacity and rate capability, is the major bottleneck to future development.  Here we propose a performance-oriented electrode structure, which is 1D nanostructure arrays with large-scale high ordering, good vertical alignment, and large interval spacing.  Benefiting from these structural merits, a great enhancement in electrochem. performance could be achieved.  Taking Sb as an example, we firstly report large-scale highly ordered Sb nanorod arrays with uniform large interval spacing (190 nm).  In return for this electrode design, high ion accessibility, fast electron transport, and strong electrode integrity are presented here.  Used as additive- and binder-free anodes for Na-ion batteries, Sb nanorod arrays showed a high capacity of 620 mA h g-1 at the 100th cycle with a retention of 84% up to 250 cycles at 0.2 A g-1, and a superior rate capability for delivering reversible capacities of 579.7 and 557.7 mA h g-1 at 10 and 20 A g-1, resp.  A full cell coupled by a P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 cathode and a Sb nanorod array anode was also constructed, which showed good cycle performance up to 250 cycles, high rate capability up to 20 A g-1, and large energy d. up to 130 Wh kg-1.  These excellent electrochem. performances shall pave the way for developing more applications of Sb nanorod arrays in energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRS7y0VfakjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljnnkRN9docAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFGns7nO&amp;md5=50b74924c2a93cc137e8a9993ce641fa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA06476C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb Porous Hollow Microspheres as Advanced Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.  With different annealing time, the hollow space and the amt. of Sb inside the tube can be easily tuned by the partial evapn. of Sb.  The as-obtained Sb@C nanotubes exhibit excellent sodium storage properties.  The remarkable electrochem. performance results from the unique coaxial nanoarchitecture.  Specifically, it delivers a high specific capacity of 407 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 240 cycles.  Furthermore, a stable capacity of 240 mAh g-1 can be retained at 1.0 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles.  Most importantly, high capacities of 350 mAh g-1 and 310 mAh g-1 can be achieved at large current densities of 10 and 20 A g-1, resp., which represents the best rate performance among the reported Sb-based anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmon6HTiU9LrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljnnkRN9docAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpsVOqsrs%253D&amp;md5=19ea4b459ee66a164418399db8b12d47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201505918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Double-Walled Sb@TiO<sub>2–x</sub> Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, double-walled cryst. Sb@amorphous TiO2-x nanotubes are synthesized by the calcination of Sb2S3@TiO2 nanorods in Ar/H2 produced by the hydrolysis of tetra-Bu titanate (TBOT) on Sb2S3 nanorods.                         rightTab-cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Sb/Sb2O3 Anode Materials Using a Polypyrrole Nanowire Network for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nam, Do-Hwan; Hong, Kyung-Sik; Lim, Sung-Jin; Kim, Min-Joong; Kwon, Hyuk-Sang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional porous Sb/Sb2O3 anode materials are successfully fabricated using a simple electrodeposition method with a polypyrrole nanowire network.  The Sb/Sb2O3-PPy electrode exhibits excellent cycle performance and outstanding rate capabilities; the charge capacity is sustained at 512.01 mAh g-1 over 100 cycles, and 56.7% of the charge capacity at a c.d. of 66 mA g-1 is retained at 3300 mA g-1.  The improved electrochem. performance of the Sb/Sb2O3-PPy electrode is attributed not only to the use of a highly porous polypyrrole nanowire network as a substrate but also to the buffer effects of the Sb2O3 matrix on the vol. expansion of Sb.  Ex situ SEM observation confirms that the Sb/Sb2O3-PPy electrode sustains a strong bond between the nanodeposits and polypyrrole nanowires even after 100 cycles, which maintains good elec. contact of Sb/Sb2O3 with the current collector without loss of the active materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqftRBwYUjUd7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljnnkRN9docAg"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel 3D ZnSb nanowire balls composed of ultra-thin nanowires were achieved through simple self-assembly method based on typical thermodn. in chem. vapor deposition (CVD) system.  The elliptic cylinder-shaped nanowires with cross-section size of ∼25nm × ∼ 10 nm display impressive performance in sodium-ion battery (SIB) application as anode material.  Comparing to pure Sb, ZnSb is advantageous in resisting huge vol. change and possess enhanced cond., which would do much better to offer a long-time cycling stability and rate performance.  Such a small size of the low dimensional structures can further improve the electron/ion transfer efficiency.  Through systematic measurements, we found that, at 20 mA/g, the capacity remains 377mAh/g after the 100th cycle with the coulombic efficiency at ∼99%.  Even if the c.d. increased to 750 mA/g, the value was still higher than 225mAh/g.  The half-cell device also provides a rapid response and stable output in the rate tests (20-650 mA/g).  The good performance originates from the unique structural configuration, implying the huge potential value of ZnSb in SIB application.  We hope the results also can expand the Sb based anode material family.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQUrzEtgymvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBnmxcbKaRAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVags7nN&amp;md5=6e34b0d48afed2593cd6f95a6751d7e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.04.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Glucose-Assisted Synthesis of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C Composite as an Electrode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, Na3V2(PO4)3 with a rhombohedral, Na+ superionic conductor (NASICON)-type structure, was synthesized via a solid-state carbothermal redn. reaction assisted by mechanochem. activation.  Electron microscopy anal. showed that the synthesized Na3V2(PO4)3 particles had an av. size of 300 nm, being coated with a uniform layer of carbon 3 nm in thickness.  As a cathode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 98.17 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 2.5 to 3.8 V.  This was owing to the V3+/V4+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaV2(PO4)3.  The cathode lost 4.92% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  As an anode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 63.2 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 1.0 to 2.5 V.  This was owing to the V2+/V3+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and Na4V2(PO4)3.  The anode lost approx. 5.41% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  The three-dimensional channel structure of NaV2(PO4)3 and the changes induced in its lattice parameters during the charge/discharge processes were simulated on the basis of d. functional theory.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqL5W7t4QuZY7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBnmxcbKaRAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXps12lsbk%253D&amp;md5=59ad73ad234d3ab597038123cdf3347c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcat.2010.02.031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guan, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel Synthetic Approach to Synthesizing Bulk and Supported Metal Phosphides</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.  The proven conversion reaction between sodium and iron sulfide results in high capacity but severe vol. changes.  Nanostructural design, including of nanosized iron sulfide yolks (∼170 nm) with porous carbon shells (∼30 nm) and extra void space (∼20 nm) in between, has been used to achieve excellent cycling performance without sacrificing capacity.  This sustainable sodium-iron sulfide battery is a promising candidate for stationary energy storage.         </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2, well known for its photocatalytic properties, has also been studied as a safer anode material for lithium ion batteries compared to graphite.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rational design and delicate control on the component, structure, and surface of electrodes in lithium-ion batteries are highly important to their performances in practical applications.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A surfactant-templated approach was used to synthesize phosphated mesoporous titanium dioxide by incorporating phosphorus from phosphoric acid directly into the framework of TiO2.  The resulting materials were characterized by XRD, nitrogen adsorption, TEM, XPS anal., UV-vis spectroscopy, FT-IR spectroscopy, and isoelec. point measurements.  The surface area of phosphated mesoporous TiO2 exceeded 300 m2/g after calcination at 400 °C.  It was found that the incorporation of phosphorus could stabilize the TiO2 framework and increase the surface area significantly.  This stabilization is attributed to two reasons: the more complete condensation of surface Ti-OH in the as-prepd. sample and the inhibition of grain growth of the embedded anatase TiO2 by the interspersed amorphous titanium phosphate matrix during thermal treatment.  Both pure and phosphated mesoporous TiO2 show significant activities on the oxidn. of n-pentane.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A layer-by-layer adsorption and reaction method was developed for the prepn. of titanium phosphate ultrathin films.  By repetitive adsorption of hydrated titanium from aq. Ti(SO4)2 soln. and subsequent reaction with phosphate groups, ultrathin films of titanium phosphate were fabricated.
